1. Introduction  Celery (Apium graveolens) is a widely used vegetable known for its crisp texture, distinct flavor, and numerous health benefits. It belongs to the Apiaceae family, which includes carrots, parsley, and fennel. Used both raw and cooked, celery is a staple in many global cuisines and is often praised for its low calorie content and high water content.  â¸»  2. History of Celery  Celery has been cultivated for thousands of years.  Ancient Use 	â€¢	Celery seeds have been found in Egyptian tombs dating back to 1300 BCE. 	â€¢	The Greeks and Romans used celery for medicinal purposes, associating it with health and strength. 	â€¢	In ancient China, celery was valued for its cooling properties.  Medieval and Renaissance Eras 	â€¢	Celery was primarily used as a medicinal herb in Europe before becoming a common food ingredient. 	â€¢	By the 17th century, European gardeners developed milder-tasting varieties.  Modern Commercial Farming 	â€¢	Celery became widely cultivated in the 19th and 20th centuries, with major production in the U.S., China, and parts of Europe.  â¸»  3. Botanical Classification 	â€¢	Kingdom: Plantae 	â€¢	Order: Apiales 	â€¢	Family: Apiaceae 	â€¢	Genus: Apium 	â€¢	Species: Apium graveolens  Celery is a biennial plant that grows best in cool, moist climates. It has a long growing season and requires careful irrigation.  â¸»  4. Cultivation and Farming  Growing Conditions 	â€¢	Climate: Celery thrives in temperate regions with moderate rainfall. 	â€¢	Soil: Prefers rich, well-draining soil with a pH of 6.0â€“6.5. 	â€¢	Sunlight: Requires full sun but can tolerate partial shade. 	â€¢	Watering: High water needs; requires consistent moisture to prevent toughness.  Farming Techniques 	â€¢	Traditional Farming: Grown in open fields with irrigation systems. 	â€¢	Hydroponic Cultivation: Some modern farms use hydroponics to produce pesticide-free celery. 	â€¢	Organic Farming: Increasing demand for pesticide-free celery has led to more organic farming methods.  â¸»  5. Types and Varieties of Celery  Celery comes in different forms, including: 	1.	Pascal Celery â€“ The most common variety, found in supermarkets worldwide. 	2.	Leaf Celery (Chinese Celery) â€“ Smaller stalks, stronger flavor; commonly used in Asian cuisine. 	3.	Celeriac (Celery Root) â€“ Grown for its edible root, used in soups and stews. 	4.	Golden Celery â€“ A rare variety with yellowish stalks.  â¸»  6. Nutritional Composition  Celery is a nutrient-dense, low-calorie vegetable.  Nutrients per 100g of Raw Celery 	â€¢	Calories: 14 kcal 	â€¢	Water Content: 95% 	â€¢	Carbohydrates: 3g 	â€¢	Fiber: 1.6g 	â€¢	Protein: 0.7g 	â€¢	Vitamin K: 37% of Daily Value 	â€¢	Vitamin C: 5% of Daily Value 	â€¢	Potassium: 260mg  Celery also contains antioxidants such as flavonoids and polyphenols, which contribute to its health benefits.  â¸»  7. Health Benefits of Celery  Celery offers numerous health benefits: 	1.	Aids Digestion â€“ High fiber content promotes gut health. 	2.	Supports Heart Health â€“ Reduces blood pressure and cholesterol levels. 	3.	Anti-Inflammatory Properties â€“ Contains antioxidants that help reduce inflammation. 	4.	Hydration Boost â€“ High water content keeps the body hydrated. 	5.	Weight Loss Friendly â€“ Low-calorie and high-fiber content make it a popular diet food.  â¸»  8. Medicinal Uses and Traditional Remedies  Celery has been used in traditional medicine for centuries: 	â€¢	Chinese Medicine: Used to cool the body and improve circulation. 	â€¢	Ayurveda: Prescribed for digestive issues and joint pain. 	â€¢	Western Herbal Medicine: Celery seed extract is used as a diuretic and anti-inflammatory agent.  â¸»  9. Celery in Culinary Traditions  Celery is used in a variety of cuisines worldwide: 	â€¢	France: Key ingredient in mirepoix (celery, onion, carrot) for soups and stews. 	â€¢	Italy: Used in soffritto as a base for many dishes. 	â€¢	China: Stir-fried with meats and tofu. 	â€¢	USA: Commonly eaten raw with dips or in salads.  â¸»  10. Celery in Modern Cuisine and Beverages  Celery is also popular in modern cooking: 	â€¢	Juices & Smoothies â€“ Celery juice is a health trend. 	â€¢	Cocktails â€“ Celery is a garnish for Bloody Mary cocktails. 	â€¢	Celery Salt â€“ Used as a seasoning in many dishes.  â¸»  11. Economic and Agricultural Impact  Celery is a billion-dollar industry, with major producers including: 	â€¢	China â€“ Largest global producer. 	â€¢	United States â€“ Major exporter, particularly from California. 	â€¢	Spain & Italy â€“ Significant European producers.  Celery farming is labor-intensive due to hand-harvesting methods.  â¸»  12. Celery in Popular Culture  Celery has appeared in various cultural references: 	â€¢	Cartoons â€“ Used as comedic props in shows like Looney Tunes. 	â€¢	Health Trends â€“ Promoted by celebrities in juicing diets. 	â€¢	Myths â€“ Some believe celery has negative calories (though not scientifically proven).  â¸»  13. Scientific Studies on Celery  Recent studies suggest celery contains compounds that: 	â€¢	Reduce inflammation. 	â€¢	Lower blood pressure. 	â€¢	Aid in cancer prevention.  Apigenin, a compound in celery, is being studied for its potential anti-cancer properties.  â¸»  14. Celery Allergies and Risks 	â€¢	Some people experience celery allergies, which can be severe. 	â€¢	Celery contains psoralens, making the skin more sensitive to sunlight.  â¸»  15. Celery as a Superfood Trend  Celery has gained popularity due to: 	â€¢	The celery juice movement, promoted for detoxification. 	â€¢	Increased focus on plant-based diets.  â¸»  16. Fun Facts About Celery 	â€¢	Ancient Romans believed celery brought good luck. 	â€¢	A stick of celery is 95% water but provides essential nutrients. 	â€¢	Celery was once considered an aphrodisiac.  â¸»  17. Conclusion  Celery is more than just a crunchy snackâ€”it has a rich history, diverse culinary uses, and significant health benefits. Whether used in cooking, medicine, or health trends, celery remains one of the most versatile vegetables in the world.

In 2023, at McDonald's joint, A celebration stirred with joyful point. Grimace's birthday, a bash to partake, With a birthday shake, he aimed to make.  But alas, a trend swept the land, On a social platform, TikTok's grand. People pretended, with fear in their eyes, That Grimace's shake would lead to demise.  They filmed reactions with dramatic flair, Claiming the shake would bring them despair. But fear not, dear friends, for it was all a jest, A TikTok challenge to put minds to the test.  Grimace, the lovable, purple friend, Was baffled by the trend and its strange blend. He knew his shake contained no harm or threat, Just sweet goodness that one shouldn't forget.  The videos spread like wildfire's dance, Creating a frenzy, fueled by happenstance. But deep down, people knew it was a bluff, For Grimace's shake was never that rough.  McDonald's stood strong amidst the craze, Assuring customers, in steadfast ways, That their beloved shake was perfectly fine, A delicacy to savor, a taste so divine.  So let us rejoice on Grimace's special day, With a shake in hand, we'll joyfully sway, For TikTok trends may come and go, But McDonald's goodness will always glow.
